TITLE      Discovery of the Origin of the Enormous 88Zr           14847001    3 
           Neutron-Capture Cross Section and Quantifying Its      14847001    4 
           Impact on Applications                                 14847001    5 
AUTHOR     (A.Stamatopoulos,P.E.Koehler,B.Digiovine,V.Mocko,      14847001    6 
           A.Matyskin,Ch.Vermeulen,A.Couture,A.Cooper,J.Morrell,  14847001    7 
           E.O'Brien)                                             14847001    8 
REFERENCE  (J,PRL,134,112702,2025) Main reference.                14847001    9 
           #doi:10.1103/PhysRevLett.134.112702                    14847001   10 
           (J,PR/C,111,034613,2025) Experimental details.         14847001   11 
           #doi:10.1103/PhysRevC.111.034613                       14847001   12 
INSTITUTE  (1USALAS,1USAPSU)                                      14847001   13 
FACILITY   (LINAC,1USALAS) Device for indirect capture            14847001   14 
           experiments on radionuclides (DICER) instrument at     14847001   15 
           the Los Alamos Neutrons Science Center (LANSCE).       14847001   16 
INC-SOURCE A white source of neutrons for this system, spanning   14847001   17 
           the energy range from below thermal to above 1 MeV,    14847001   18 
           is produced when the pulsed 800 MeV proton beam from   14847001   19 
           the LANSCE linac impinges on the new Mark-IV           14847001   20 
           neutron-production target.                             14847001   21 
DETECTOR   (GLASD,HPGE) 6Li-glass scintillators and               14847001   22 
           photomultiplier tubes. Backgrounds due to in-beam      14847001   23 
           gamma rays and scattered neutrons were measured and    14847001   24 
           subtracted. HPGe detector was used for the sample      14847001   25 
           characterization only.                                 14847001   26 
SAMPLE     The 88Zr was produced by irradiating an yttrium metal  14847001   27 
           target at the isotope production facility (IPF) at     14847001   28 
           LANSCE. The 88Zr was separated from the IPF            14847001   29 
           production target and fabricated into a sample in a    14847001   30 
           hot cell. To ensure a uniform amount of 88Zr across    14847001   31 
           the area of the neutron beam (1 mm diameter), the      14847001   32 
           88Zr was dissolved in hydrochloric acid (HCl) before   14847001   33 
           being loaded into the sample container. The amount of  14847001   34 
           88Zr in the sample (825+-33 MBq) was determined by     14847001   35 
           gamma-ray spectroscopy using a high-purity germanium   14847001   36 
           detector to count the decay gamma rays from its        14847001   37 
           daughter 88Y relative to 88Y standards that fabricated.14847001   38 
            Container dimensions were measured with a precision   14847001   39 
           inspection device. In this way, the areal density of   14847001   40 
           the sample was determined to be (7.44+-0.22)*10**-7    14847001   41 
           atoms of 88Zr per barn. A sample-out or blank sample   14847001   42 
           was fabricated by dispensing HCl into a second         14847001   43 
           container.                                             14847001   44 
METHOD     (TOF) Neutron energy is determined using the time-of-  14847001   45 
           flight technique. The transmission data for the 88Zr   14847001   46 
           sample can be converted to total cross section sigmat  14847001   47 
           = (ln(1/T88))/n, and numerically integrated above      14847001   48 
           Ecut=0.5 eV to obtain an estimate of the resonance     14847001   49 
           integral.                                              14847001   50 
STATUS     (APRVD) Approved by A.Stamatopoulos on March 27, 2025. 14847001   51

ERR-ANALYS (ERR-S) 1 standard-deviation statistical uncertainties.14847002    4 
CORRECTION Unfortunately, somewhat different amounts of HCl were  14847002    5 
           dispensed into the sample-in (7.8 mg) and sample-out   14847002    6 
            (8.1 mg) containers for 88Zr and there also was a     14847002    7 
           small difference (0.02 mm) between the inner           14847002    8 
           diameters of these containers. A correction to the     14847002    9 
           88Zr transmission, for these differences was           14847002   10 
           calculated using the measured weights and diameters,   14847002   11 
           and transmission data we obtained for the HCl sample.  14847002   12 
           This correction factor ranged from 0.85 at thermal     14847002   13 
           energy to 0.97 at 1 keV.                               14847002   14

REACTION  1(40-ZR-88(N,0),,EN)                                    14847003    3

ANALYSIS   The R-matrix formalism is a well-known technique for   14847003    6 
           fitting neutron transmission data and obtaining        14847003    7 
           resonance parameters. These parameters can then be     14847003    8 
           used to extract the neutron-capture cross section. At  14847003    9 
           these low energies, only two reactions are possible,   14847003   10 
           neutron scattering and neutron capture. Therefore,     14847003   11 
           each resonance has three parameters, its energy (E),   14847003   12 
           neutron width (Gn), and gamma radiation width (Ggamma).14847003   13 
           Once these parameters are determined by fitting        14847003   14 
           transmission data, they can be used to calculate the   14847003   15 
           capture cross section.                                 14847003   16 
ERR-ANALYS (DATA-ERR) Fitting uncertainties that include 1        14847003   17 
           standard-deviation statistical uncertainties.          14847003   18 
FLAG       (1.) Fixed value for elastic width in subthreshold     14847003   19 
            (negative energy) resonance.                          14847003   20
